vi</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">Reference</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://whc.unesco.org/en/list/422">422</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">Inscription</th><td>\n2017 <small>(41st <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">Session</a>)</small></td></tr>\n\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Lake District</b>, also known as <b>the Lakes</b> or <b>Lakeland</b>, is a mountainous region in <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West England</a>. A popular holiday destination, it is famous for its lakes, forests and mountains (or <i><a href="/wiki/Fells" class="mw-redirect" title="Fells">fells</a></i>), and its associations with <a href="/wiki/William_Wordsworth" title="William Wordsworth">William Wordsworth</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Lake_Poets" title="Lake Poets">Lake Poets</a> and also with <a href="/wiki/Beatrix_Potter" title="Beatrix Potter">Beatrix Potter</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Ruskin" title="John Ruskin">John Ruskin</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_England_and_Wales" title="National parks of England and Wales">National Park</a> was established in 1951 and covers an area of 2,362 square kilometres.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It was designated a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Lake District is located entirely within the county of <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>. All the land in England higher than 3,000 feet (914&#160;m) above sea level lies within the National Park, including <a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a>, the highest mountain in England.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It also contains the deepest and longest bodies of water in England, <a href="/wiki/Wast_Water" title="Wast Water">Wast Water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Southern_Fells"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.7</span> <span class="toctext">Southern Fells</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Southeastern_area"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.8</span> <span class="toctext">Southeastern area</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Lakes"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Lakes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Wildlife"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Wildlife</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Agriculture_and_forestry"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Agriculture and forestry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Industry"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Industry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Development_of_tourism"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Development of tourism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Gastronomy"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Gastronomy</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Literature_and_art"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Literature and art</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Nomenclature"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Nomenclature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lake_District_National_Park">Lake District National Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Lake District National Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png/200px-National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png" width="200" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png/300px-National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png 2x" data-file-width="377" data-file-height="447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lake District National Park (shown as number 2) in a map of national parks in England and Wales.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Lake District National Park</b> includes all of the central Lake District, though the town of <a href="/wiki/Kendal" title="Kendal">Kendal</a>, some coastal areas, and the Lakeland Peninsulas are outside the park boundary.\n</p><p>The area was designated a <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_England_and_Wales" title="National parks of England and Wales">national park</a> on 9 May 1951 (less than a month after the first UK national park designation \xe2\x80\x94 the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a>).  It retained its original boundaries until 2016 when it was extended by 3% in the direction of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales_National_Park" title="Yorkshire Dales National Park">Yorkshire Dales National Park</a> to incorporate areas such as land of high landscape value in the <a href="/wiki/Lune_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Lune Valley">Lune Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is the most visited national park in the United Kingdom with 15.8&#160;million annual visitors and more than 23&#160;million annual day visits,<sup id="cite_ref-facts_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> the largest of the thirteen national parks in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, and the second largest in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Cairngorms" title="Cairngorms">Cairngorms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Its aim is to protect the landscape by restricting unwelcome change by industry or commerce. Most of the land in the park is in private ownership, with about 55% registered as agricultural land. Landowners include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Individual farmers and other private landowners, with more than half of the agricultural land farmed by the owners.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust</a> owns about a quarter of the total area (including some lakes and land of significant landscape value).</li>\n<li>The Forestry Commission and other investors in forests and woodland.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Utilities" title="United Utilities">United Utilities</a> owns 8%</li>\n<li>Lake District National Park Authority (3.9%)</li></ul>\n<p>The National Park Authority is based at offices in <a href="/wiki/Kendal" title="Kendal">Kendal</a>. It runs a visitor centre on <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a> at a former country house called <a href="/wiki/Brockhole_Lake_District_Visitor_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Brockhole Lake District Visitor Centre">Brockhole</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Coniston Boating Centre,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and Information Centres. It is reducing its landholding.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In common with all other national parks in England, there is no restriction on entry to, or movement within the park along public routes, but access to cultivated land is usually restricted to <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_way_in_England_and_Wales" title="Rights of way in England and Wales">public footpaths</a>, bridleways and byways. Much of the uncultivated land has statutory open access rights, which cover around 50% of the park.\n</p><p>The lakes and mountains combine to form impressive scenery. Farmland and settlement have altered the natural scenery, and the ecology has been modified by human influence for <a href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">millennia</a> and includes important <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_habitat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildlife habitat">wildlife habitats</a>. Having failed in a previous attempt to gain World Heritage status as a natural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, because of human activities, it was eventually successful in the category of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_landscape" title="Cultural landscape">cultural landscape</a> and was awarded the status in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_geography">Human geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Human geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_District_Map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Lake_District_Map.PNG/220px-Lake_District_Map.PNG" width="220" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Lake_District_Map.PNG/330px-Lake_District_Map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Lake_District_Map.PNG/440px-Lake_District_Map.PNG 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="569" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_District_Map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The location of the Lake District, and approximate extent, shown in white, within <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The precise extent of the Lake District was not defined traditionally, but is slightly larger than that of the National Park<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, the total area of which is about 912 square miles (2,362&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The park extends just over 32 miles (51&#160;km) from east to west and nearly 40 miles (64&#160;km) from north to south,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> with areas such as the Lake District Peninsulas to the south lying outside the National Park.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Lake District is one of the most highly populated national parks. There are, however, only a handful of major settlements within this mountainous area, the towns of <a href="/wiki/Keswick,_Cumbria" title="Keswick, Cumbria">Keswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windermere,_Cumbria_(town)" title="Windermere, Cumbria (town)">Windermere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambleside" title="Ambleside">Ambleside</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bowness-on-Windermere" title="Bowness-on-Windermere">Bowness-on-Windermere</a> being the four largest. Significant towns immediately outside the boundary of the national park include <a href="/wiki/Millom" title="Millom">Millom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness" title="Barrow-in-Furness">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendal" title="Kendal">Kendal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulverston" title="Ulverston">Ulverston</a>, Dalton-in-Furness, <a href="/wiki/Cockermouth" title="Cockermouth">Cockermouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penrith,_Cumbria" title="Penrith, Cumbria">Penrith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grange-over-Sands" title="Grange-over-Sands">Grange-over-Sands</a>; each of these has important economic links with the area. Villages such as <a href="/wiki/Coniston,_Cumbria" title="Coniston, Cumbria">Coniston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Threlkeld" title="Threlkeld">Threlkeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glenridding" title="Glenridding">Glenridding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pooley_Bridge" title="Pooley Bridge">Pooley Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broughton-in-Furness" title="Broughton-in-Furness">Broughton-in-Furness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grasmere" title="Grasmere">Grasmere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newby_Bridge" title="Newby Bridge">Newby Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staveley,_Cumbria" title="Staveley, Cumbria">Staveley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lindale,_Cumbria" title="Lindale, Cumbria">Lindale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gosforth,_Cumbria" title="Gosforth, Cumbria">Gosforth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawkshead" title="Hawkshead">Hawkshead</a> are more local centres. The economies of almost all are intimately linked with tourism. Beyond these are a scattering of hamlets and many isolated farmsteads, some of which are still tied to agriculture; others now function as part of the tourist economy.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A591_road,_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg/220px-A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg/330px-A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg/440px-A591_road%2C_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="2573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A591_road,_Lake_District_-_June_2009_Edit_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The A591 road as it passes through the countryside between Ambleside and Grasmere</div></div></div>\n<p>The Lake District National Park is almost contained within a box of <a href="/wiki/Trunk_road" title="Trunk road">trunk routes</a>. It is flanked to the east by the <a href="/wiki/A6_road_(England)" title="A6 road (England)">A6 road</a> which runs from Kendal to Penrith (though the extension approved in 2015 is east of the A6). The <a href="/wiki/A590_road" title="A590 road">A590</a> which connects the M6 to <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness" title="Barrow-in-Furness">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/A5092_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A5092 road">A5092</a> trunk roads cut across its southern fringes and the <a href="/wiki/A66_road" title="A66 road">A66</a> trunk road between Penrith and <a href="/wiki/Workington" title="Workington">Workington</a> cuts across its northern edge. Finally the <a href="/wiki/A595_road" title="A595 road">A595</a> trunk road runs through the coastal plains to the west of the area, linking the A66 with the A5092.\n</p><p>Besides these, a few <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">A roads</a> penetrate the area itself, notably the <a href="/wiki/A591" class="mw-redirect" title="A591">A591</a> which runs north-westwards from Kendal to Windermere and then on to Keswick. It continues up the east side of <a href="/wiki/Bassenthwaite_Lake" title="Bassenthwaite Lake">Bassenthwaite Lake</a>. "The A591, Grasmere, Lake District" was short-listed in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Google_Street_View" title="Google Street View">Google Street View</a> awards in the Most Romantic Street category. The <a href="/wiki/A593_road" title="A593 road">A593</a> and <a href="/wiki/A5084_road_(Great_Britain)#Four-digit_roads_(50xx)" class="mw-redirect" title="A5084 road (Great Britain)">A5084</a> link the Ambleside and Coniston areas with the A590 to the south whilst the <a href="/wiki/A592_road" title="A592 road">A592</a> and <a href="/wiki/A5074_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A5074 road">A5074</a> similarly link Windermere with the A590. The A592 also continues northwards from Windermere to <a href="/wiki/Ullswater" title="Ullswater">Ullswater</a> and Penrith by way of the <a href="/wiki/Kirkstone_Pass" title="Kirkstone Pass">Kirkstone Pass</a>.\n</p><p>Some valleys which are not penetrated by A roads are served by <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">B roads</a>. The B5289 serves Lorton Vale and <a href="/wiki/Buttermere,_Cumbria" title="Buttermere, Cumbria">Buttermere</a> and links via the <a href="/wiki/Honister_Pass" title="Honister Pass">Honister Pass</a> with <a href="/wiki/Borrowdale" title="Borrowdale">Borrowdale</a>. The <a href="/wiki/B5292_road" class="mw-redirect" title="B5292 road">B5292</a> ascends the <a href="/wiki/Whinlatter_Pass" title="Whinlatter Pass">Whinlatter Pass</a> from Lorton Vale before dropping down to <a href="/wiki/Braithwaite" title="Braithwaite">Braithwaite</a> near Keswick. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=B5322_road&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="B5322 road (page does not exist)">B5322</a> serves the valley of <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_in_the_Vale" title="St John&#39;s in the Vale">St John\'s in the Vale</a> whilst <a href="/wiki/Great_Langdale" title="Great Langdale">Great Langdale</a> is served by the <a href="/wiki/B5343_road" class="mw-redirect" title="B5343 road">B5343</a>. Other valleys such as <a href="/wiki/Little_Langdale" title="Little Langdale">Little Langdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eskdale,_Cumbria" title="Eskdale, Cumbria">Eskdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duddon_Valley" title="Duddon Valley">Dunnerdale</a> are served by minor roads. The last of these is connected with the first two by the <a href="/wiki/Wrynose_Pass" title="Wrynose Pass">Wrynose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hardknott_Pass" title="Hardknott Pass">Hardknott</a> passes respectively; both of these passes are known for their steep gradients and are together one of the most popular <a href="/wiki/Climbing_specialist" title="Climbing specialist">climbs</a> in the United Kingdom for cycling enthusiasts.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> A minor road through the <a href="/wiki/Newlands_Valley" title="Newlands Valley">Newlands Valley</a> connects via <a href="/wiki/Newlands_Hause" class="mw-redirect" title="Newlands Hause">Newlands Hause</a> with the B5289 at Buttermere. <a href="/wiki/Wasdale" title="Wasdale">Wasdale</a> is served by a cul-de-sac minor road, as are <a href="/wiki/Longsleddale" title="Longsleddale">Longsleddale</a> and the valleys at <a href="/wiki/Haweswater_Reservoir" title="Haweswater Reservoir">Haweswater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kentmere" title="Kentmere">Kentmere</a>. There are networks of minor roads in the lower-lying southern part of the area, connecting numerous communities between Kendal, Windermere and Coniston.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways_and_ferries">Railways and ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Railways and ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> skirts the eastern edge of the Lake District and the <a href="/wiki/Cumbrian_Coast_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Cumbrian Coast Line">Cumbrian Coast Line</a> passes through the southern and western fringes of the area. A single railway line, the <a href="/wiki/Windermere_Branch_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Windermere Branch Line">Windermere Branch Line</a>, penetrates from Kendal to Windermere via Staveley. Railways once served Broughton-in-Furness and Coniston (closed to passengers in 1958) and another ran from Penrith to Cockermouth via Keswick (closed west of Keswick in 1966 and completely in 1972). Part of the track of the latter is used by the improved A66 trunk road.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cumbrian_Coast_line" title="Cumbrian Coast line">Cumbrian Coast line</a> has three stations within the boundaries of the national park (and additionally <a href="/wiki/Drigg" title="Drigg">Drigg</a>, about a third of a mile from the park boundary). The line gives railway enthusiasts and others a flavour of a pre-<a href="/wiki/Beeching_cuts" title="Beeching cuts">Beeching</a> railway line, with features like manually operated level crossing gates, as well as giving a good connection to the steam railway into Eskdale and providing access for cyclists and serious walkers to the Western Fells.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The narrow gauge <a href="/wiki/Ravenglass_and_Eskdale_Railway" title="Ravenglass and Eskdale Railway">Ravenglass and Eskdale Railway</a> runs from <a href="/wiki/Ravenglass" title="Ravenglass">Ravenglass</a> on the west coast up Eskdale as far as Dalegarth Station near the hamlet of Boot, catering for tourists. Another <a href="/wiki/Heritage_railway" title="Heritage railway">heritage railway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_and_Haverthwaite_Railway" title="Lakeside and Haverthwaite Railway">Lakeside and Haverthwaite Railway</a>, runs between Lake Windermere and <a href="/wiki/Haverthwaite" title="Haverthwaite">Haverthwaite</a>, and tourists can connect at Lakeside with the boats up the lake to Bowness.\n</p><p>A vehicle-carrying <a href="/wiki/Cable_ferry" title="Cable ferry">cable ferry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Windermere_Ferry" title="Windermere Ferry">Windermere Ferry</a>, runs frequent services across Windermere. There are also seasonal passenger boats on Coniston Water, Derwent Water and Ullswater.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Footpaths_and_bridleways">Footpaths and bridleways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Footpaths and bridleways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There are many paths over which the public has a <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_way_in_England_and_Wales" title="Rights of way in England and Wales">right of way</a>, all of which should be signposted. Within the area of the National Park in 2012 there were 2,159&#160;km (1,342&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Public_footpath_(England_and_Wales)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public footpath (England and Wales)">public footpaths</a>,\n875&#160;km (544&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Public_bridleway_(England_and_Wales)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public bridleway (England and Wales)">public bridleways</a>,\n15&#160;km (9&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Restricted_byway" class="mw-redirect" title="Restricted byway">restricted byways</a> and\n30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Byway_open_to_all_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Byway open to all traffic">byways open to all traffic</a>. There is also a general "<a href="/wiki/Countryside_and_Rights_of_Way_Act_2000" title="Countryside and Rights of Way Act 2000">right to roam</a>" in open country.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many of these tracks arose centuries ago and were used either as ridge highways (such as along <a href="/wiki/High_Street_(Lake_District)" title="High Street (Lake District)">High Street</a>) or as <a href="/wiki/List_of_hill_passes_of_the_Lake_District" title="List of hill passes of the Lake District">passes for travelling across the ridges</a> between settlements in the valleys. Historically these paths were not planned for reaching summits, but more recently they are used by fell walkers for that purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-ihc_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ihc-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cycling and horse riding are allowed on bridleways, but cyclists must give way to all other users. Motor vehicles are only allowed on "byways open to all traffic" (<a href="/wiki/Green_lane_(road)" title="Green lane (road)">green lanes</a>) but in practice Traffic Regulation Orders have been brought in on several prohibiting motor traffic, although a system of permits operates on <a href="/wiki/Gatesgarth_Pass" class="mw-redirect" title="Gatesgarth Pass">Gatesgarth Pass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:3008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg" class="image" title="A panorama from the summit of Scafell Pike, August 2007"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg/3000px-Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg" width="3000" height="283" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg/4500px-Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg/6000px-Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="12931" data-file-height="1220" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Annotated_Scafel_Pike_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Annotated Scafel Pike Panorama.jpg"> </a></div>A panorama from the summit of Scafell Pike, August 2007</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>As the highest ground in England, <a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a> naturally has a very extensive view on a clear day, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Mountains" title="Mourne Mountains">Mourne Mountains</a> in Northern Ireland to <a href="/wiki/Snowdonia" title="Snowdonia">Snowdonia</a> in Wales. The Lake District takes the form of a roughly circular upland massif deeply dissected by a broadly <a href="/wiki/Radial_drainage" class="mw-redirect" title="Radial drainage">radial pattern</a> of major valleys whose character is largely the product of repeated <a href="/wiki/Ice_ages" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice ages">glaciations</a> over the last 2&#160;million years. Most of these valleys display the U-shaped cross-section characteristic of glacial origin, and often contain elongate lakes occupying sizeable <a href="/wiki/Bedrock" title="Bedrock">bedrock</a> hollows, often with tracts of relatively flat ground at their heads. Smaller lakes known as <a href="/wiki/Tarn_(lake)" title="Tarn (lake)">tarns</a> occupy <a href="/wiki/Cirque_(landform)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cirque (landform)">glacial cirques</a> at higher elevations. It is the abundance of both which has led to the area becoming known as the Lake District.\n</p><p>The mountains of the Lake District are also known as the "Cumbrian Mountains", although this name is less frequently used than terms like "the Lake District" or "the Lakeland Fells". Many of the higher <a href="/wiki/Fell" title="Fell">fells</a> are rocky, while <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> predominates at lower altitudes. Vegetation cover across better drained areas includes <a href="/wiki/Bracken" title="Bracken">bracken</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna">heather</a>, though much of the land is <a href="/wiki/Bog" title="Bog">boggy</a>, due to the high rainfall. Deciduous native woodland occurs on many steeper slopes below the <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a>, but with native oak supplemented by extensive conifer plantations in many areas, particularly <a href="/wiki/Grizedale_Forest" title="Grizedale Forest">Grizedale Forest</a> in the generally lower southern part of the area.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wasdale_screes.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of the Wasdale screes descending into Wastwater, the deepest lake in England."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Wasdale_screes.jpg/1000px-Wasdale_screes.jpg" width="1000" height="273" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Wasdale_screes.jpg/1500px-Wasdale_screes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/Wasdale_screes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1990" data-file-height="543" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wasdale_screes.jpg" title="File:Wasdale screes.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of the Wasdale screes descending into Wastwater, the deepest lake in England.</div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Valleys">Valleys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Valleys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Tongue_Valley_(looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike),_near_Troutbeck,_Cumbria,_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park,_United_Kingdom,_Europe_(November_2008).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg/220px-The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg/330px-The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg/440px-The_Tongue_Valley_%28looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike%29%2C_near_Troutbeck%2C_Cumbria%2C_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park%2C_United_Kingdom%2C_Europe_%28November_2008%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Tongue_Valley_(looking_from_Dollywaggon_Pike),_near_Troutbeck,_Cumbria,_at_the_Lake_District_National_Park,_United_Kingdom,_Europe_(November_2008).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tongue Valley (looking from <i>Dollywaggon Pike</i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>The principal radial valleys are (clockwise from the south) <a href="/wiki/Dunnerdale" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunnerdale">Dunnerdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eskdale,_Cumbria" title="Eskdale, Cumbria">Eskdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wasdale" title="Wasdale">Wasdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ennerdale_Water" title="Ennerdale Water">Ennerdale</a>, Lorton Vale and the <a href="/wiki/Buttermere" title="Buttermere">Buttermere</a> valley, the <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent,_Cumbria" title="River Derwent, Cumbria">Derwent Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borrowdale" title="Borrowdale">Borrowdale</a>, the valleys containing Ullswater and Haweswater, <a href="/wiki/Longsleddale" title="Longsleddale">Longsleddale</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kentmere" title="Kentmere">Kentmere</a> valley and those radiating from the head of Windermere including <a href="/wiki/Great_Langdale" title="Great Langdale">Great Langdale</a>. The valleys break the mountains up into separate blocks, which have been described by various authors in different ways. The most frequently encountered approach is that made popular by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wainwright" title="Alfred Wainwright">Alfred Wainwright</a> who published seven separate area guides to the Lakeland Fells.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Woodlands">Woodlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Woodlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Below the <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a> are wooded areas, including British and European native <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> woodlands and introduced softwood plantations. The woodlands provide habitats for native English wildlife. The native <a href="/wiki/Red_squirrel" title="Red squirrel">red squirrel</a> is found in the Lake District and in a few other parts of England. In parts of the Lake District the rainfall is higher than in any other part of England. This gives <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liverwort" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverwort">liverworts</a> the chance to grow. There is some <a href="/wiki/Ancient_woodland" title="Ancient woodland">ancient woodland</a> in the National Park. Management of the woodlands varies: some are <a href="/wiki/Coppice" class="mw-redirect" title="Coppice">coppiced</a>, some <a href="/wiki/Pollarding" title="Pollarding">pollarded</a>, some left to grow naturally, and some provide grazing and shelter.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Fells_.28hills.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fells_(hills)">Fells (hills)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fells (hills)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scafell_massif.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" massif, the highest ground in England, seen over <a href="/wiki/Wasdale" title="Wasdale">Wasdale</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="noviewer thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="color:green;">Penrith</span></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:28%;left:48.571%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><img alt="Keswick" style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:4px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><span style="color:green;">Keswick</span></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:49.987%;left:65.467%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><img alt="Ambleside" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/6px-Location_dot_green.svg.png" title="Ambleside" width="6" height="6" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/9px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/12px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:4px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><span style="color:green;">Ambleside</span></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:18.493%;left:27.429%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><img alt="Cockermouth" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/6px-Location_dot_green.svg.png" title="Cockermouth" width="6" height="6" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/9px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/12px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:4px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right"><span style="color:green;">Cockermouth</span></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:56.533%;left:70.762%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><img alt="Windermere" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/6px-Location_dot_green.svg.png" title="Windermere" width="6" height="6" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/9px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/12px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:4px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><span style="color:green;">Windermere</span></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:45.588%;left:59.563%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><img alt="Grasmere" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/6px-Location_dot_green.svg.png" title="Grasmere" width="6" height="6" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/9px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Location_dot_green.svg/12px-Location_dot_green.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;bottom:4px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px"><span style="color:green;">Grasmere</span></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_District_National_Park_UK_relief_location_map.png" title="File:Lake District National Park UK relief location map.png"> </a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><b>Some major fells and towns</b></div></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fells_in_the_Lake_District" title="List of fells in the Lake District">list of fells in the Lake District</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_hills_in_the_Lake_District" title="List of hills in the Lake District">list of hills in the Lake District</a></div>\n<p>The four highest mountains in the Lake District exceed 3,000 feet (914&#160;m). These are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a>, 978&#160;m (3,209&#160;ft)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scafell" class="mw-redirect" title="Scafell">Scafell</a>, 965&#160;m (3,166&#160;ft)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Helvellyn" title="Helvellyn">Helvellyn</a>, 951&#160;m (3,120&#160;ft)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Skiddaw" title="Skiddaw">Skiddaw</a>, 931&#160;m (3,054&#160;ft)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Fells">Northern Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Northern Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Fells" title="Northern Fells">Northern Fells</a> are a clearly defined range of hills contained within a 13&#160;km (8&#160;mi) diameter circle between <a href="/wiki/Keswick,_Cumbria" title="Keswick, Cumbria">Keswick</a> in the south west and <a href="/wiki/Caldbeck" title="Caldbeck">Caldbeck</a> in the north east. They culminate in the 931&#160;m (3,054&#160;ft) peak of <a href="/wiki/Skiddaw" title="Skiddaw">Skiddaw</a>. Other notable peaks are <a href="/wiki/Blencathra" title="Blencathra">Blencathra</a> (also known as Saddleback) (868&#160;m (2,848&#160;ft)) and <a href="/wiki/Carrock_Fell" title="Carrock Fell">Carrock Fell</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bassenthwaite_Lake" title="Bassenthwaite Lake">Bassenthwaite Lake</a> occupies the valley between this massif and the North Western Fells.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Western_Fells">North Western Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: North Western Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/North_Western_Fells" title="North Western Fells">North Western Fells</a> lie between <a href="/wiki/Borrowdale" title="Borrowdale">Borrowdale</a> and Bassenthwaite Lake to the east and <a href="/wiki/Buttermere" title="Buttermere">Buttermere</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorton_Vale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lorton Vale (page does not exist)">Lorton Vale</a> to the west. Their southernmost point is at <a href="/wiki/Honister_Pass" title="Honister Pass">Honister Pass</a>. This area includes the Derwent Fells above the <a href="/wiki/Newlands_Valley" title="Newlands Valley">Newlands Valley</a> and hills to the north amongst which are <a href="/wiki/Dale_Head" title="Dale Head">Dale Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robinson_(Lake_District)" title="Robinson (Lake District)">Robinson</a>. To the north stand <a href="/wiki/Grasmoor" title="Grasmoor">Grasmoor</a>, highest in the range at 852&#160;m (2,795&#160;ft), <a href="/wiki/Grisedale_Pike" title="Grisedale Pike">Grisedale Pike</a> and the hills around the valley of <a href="/wiki/Coledale_(Cumbria)" title="Coledale (Cumbria)">Coledale</a>, and in the far north west is Thornthwaite Forest and <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Seat" title="Lord&#39;s Seat">Lord\'s Seat</a>. The fells in this area are rounded <a href="/wiki/Skiddaw_slate" class="mw-redirect" title="Skiddaw slate">Skiddaw slate</a>, with few tarns and relatively few rock faces.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Fells">Western Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Western Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg/220px-Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg/330px-Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg/440px-Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="997" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westmorland_cairn_Great_Gable.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The view from the cairn built by the Westmorland brothers in 1876 to the SW of the summit of Great Gable, which they considered the finest view in the district.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Fells" title="Western Fells">Western Fells</a> lie between Buttermere and <a href="/wiki/Wasdale" title="Wasdale">Wasdale</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Sty_Head" title="Sty Head">Sty Head</a> forming the apex of a large triangle. <a href="/wiki/Ennerdale_Water" title="Ennerdale Water">Ennerdale</a> bisects the area, which consists of the <a href="/wiki/High_Stile" title="High Stile">High Stile</a> ridge north of Ennerdale, the <a href="/wiki/Loweswater_Fells" class="mw-redirect" title="Loweswater Fells">Loweswater Fells</a> in the far north west, the <a href="/wiki/Pillar_(Lake_District)" title="Pillar (Lake District)">Pillar</a> group in the south west, and <a href="/wiki/Great_Gable" title="Great Gable">Great Gable</a> (899&#160;m (2,949&#160;ft)) near Sty Head. Other tops include <a href="/wiki/Seatallan" title="Seatallan">Seatallan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haystacks_(Lake_District)" title="Haystacks (Lake District)">Haystacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Fell" title="Kirk Fell">Kirk Fell</a>. This area is craggy and steep, with the impressive pinnacle of Pillar Rock its showpiece. <a href="/wiki/Wastwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Wastwater">Wastwater</a>, located in this part, is England\'s deepest lake.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Fells">Central Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Central Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Fells" title="Central Fells">Central Fells</a> are lower in elevation than surrounding areas of fell, peaking at 762&#160;m (2,500&#160;ft) at <a href="/wiki/High_Raise,_Langdale" class="mw-redirect" title="High Raise, Langdale">High Raise</a>. They take the form of a ridge running between <a href="/wiki/Derwent_Water" class="mw-redirect" title="Derwent Water">Derwent Water</a> in the west and <a href="/wiki/Thirlmere" title="Thirlmere">Thirlmere</a> in the east, from <a href="/wiki/Keswick,_Cumbria" title="Keswick, Cumbria">Keswick</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Langdale_Pikes" class="mw-redirect" title="Langdale Pikes">Langdale Pikes</a> in the south. A spur extends south east to <a href="/wiki/Loughrigg_Fell" title="Loughrigg Fell">Loughrigg Fell</a> above <a href="/wiki/Ambleside" title="Ambleside">Ambleside</a>. The central ridge running north over <a href="/wiki/High_Seat,_Lake_District" class="mw-redirect" title="High Seat, Lake District">High Seat</a> is exceptionally boggy.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Fells">Eastern Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Eastern Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glenridding,_Cumbria,_England_-_June_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg/220px-Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg/330px-Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg/440px-Glenridding%2C_Cumbria%2C_England_-_June_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3947" data-file-height="1941" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glenridding,_Cumbria,_England_-_June_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The village of <a href="/wiki/Glenridding" title="Glenridding">Glenridding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ullswater" title="Ullswater">Ullswater</a> lake</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Fells" title="Eastern Fells">Eastern Fells</a> consist of a long north-to-south <a href="/wiki/Ridge" title="Ridge">ridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Helvellyn_range" title="Helvellyn range">Helvellyn range</a>, running from <a href="/wiki/Clough_Head" title="Clough Head">Clough Head</a> to <a href="/wiki/Seat_Sandal" title="Seat Sandal">Seat Sandal</a> with the 950&#160;m (3,118&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Helvellyn" title="Helvellyn">Helvellyn</a> at its highest point. The western slopes of these summits tend to be grassy, with rocky <a href="/wiki/Cirque" title="Cirque">corries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cliff" title="Cliff">crags</a> on the eastern side. The <a href="/wiki/Fairfield_(Lake_District)" title="Fairfield (Lake District)">Fairfield</a> group lies to the south of the range, and forms a similar pattern with towering rock faces and hidden valleys spilling into the <a href="/wiki/Patterdale" title="Patterdale">Patterdale</a> valley. It culminates in the height of <a href="/wiki/Red_Screes" title="Red Screes">Red Screes</a> overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Kirkstone_Pass" title="Kirkstone Pass">Kirkstone Pass</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Far_Eastern_Fells">Far Eastern Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Far Eastern Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg/220px-Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg/330px-Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg/440px-Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haweswater_from_Harter_Fell_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haweswater_Reservoir" title="Haweswater Reservoir">Haweswater Reservoir</a> from <a href="/wiki/Harter_Fell_(Mardale)" title="Harter Fell (Mardale)">Harter Fell</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Far_Eastern_Fells" title="Far Eastern Fells">Far Eastern Fells</a> refer to all of the Lakeland fells to the east of Ullswater and the A592 road running south to Windermere. At 828&#160;m (2,717&#160;ft), the peak known as <a href="/wiki/High_Street_(Lake_District)" title="High Street (Lake District)">High Street</a> is the highest point on a complex ridge which runs broadly north\xe2\x80\x93south and overlooks the hidden valley of <a href="/wiki/Haweswater_Reservoir" title="Haweswater Reservoir">Haweswater</a> to its east. In the north of this region are the lower fells of Martindale Common and Bampton Common whilst in the south are the fells overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Kentmere" title="Kentmere">Kentmere</a> valley. Further to the east, beyond <a href="/wiki/Mardale" title="Mardale">Mardale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longsleddale" title="Longsleddale">Longsleddale</a> is <a href="/wiki/Shap" title="Shap">Shap</a> Fell, an extensive area consisting of high <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a>, more rolling and <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennine</a> in nature than the mountains to the west.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Fells">Southern Fells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Southern Fells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg/220px-Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg/330px-Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg/440px-Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1221" data-file-height="951" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coniston_Water_from_Holme_Fell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Coniston_Water" title="Coniston Water">Coniston Water</a> from <a href="/wiki/Holme_Fell" title="Holme Fell">Holme Fell</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Fells" title="Southern Fells">Southern Fells</a> occupy the southwestern quarter of the Lake District. They can be regarded as comprising a northern grouping between Wasdale, Eskdale and the two Langdale valleys, a southeastern group east of Dunnerdale and south of Little Langdale and a southwestern group bounded by Eskdale to the north and Dunnerdale to the east.\n</p><p>The first group includes England\'s highest mountains: <a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a> in the centre, at 978&#160;m (3,209&#160;ft) and <a href="/wiki/Scafell" class="mw-redirect" title="Scafell">Scafell</a> one mile (1.6&#160;km) to the southwest. Though it is slightly lower it has a 700&#160;ft (210&#160;m) rockface, Scafell Crag, on its northern side. It also includes the <a href="/wiki/Wastwater_Screes" class="mw-redirect" title="Wastwater Screes">Wastwater Screes</a> overlooking Wasdale, the <a href="/wiki/Glaramara" title="Glaramara">Glaramara</a> ridge overlooking Borrowdale, the three tops of <a href="/wiki/Crinkle_Crags" title="Crinkle Crags">Crinkle Crags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowfell" title="Bowfell">Bowfell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esk_Pike" title="Esk Pike">Esk Pike</a>. The core of the area is drained by the infant <a href="/wiki/River_Esk,_Cumbria" title="River Esk, Cumbria">River Esk</a>. Collectively these are some of the Lake District\'s most rugged hillsides.\n</p><p>The second group, otherwise known as the <a href="/wiki/Furness_Fells" title="Furness Fells">Furness Fells</a> or Coniston Fells, have as their northern boundary the steep and narrow  <a href="/wiki/Hardknott_Pass" title="Hardknott Pass">Hardknott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrynose_Pass" title="Wrynose Pass">Wrynose</a> passes. The highest are <a href="/wiki/Old_Man_of_Coniston" title="Old Man of Coniston">Old Man of Coniston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swirl_How" title="Swirl How">Swirl How</a> which slightly exceed 800&#160;m (2,600&#160;ft).\n</p><p>The third group to the west of the Duddon includes <a href="/wiki/Harter_Fell,_Eskdale" class="mw-redirect" title="Harter Fell, Eskdale">Harter Fell</a> and the long ridge leading over <a href="/wiki/Whitfell" title="Whitfell">Whitfell</a> to <a href="/wiki/Black_Combe" title="Black Combe">Black Combe</a> and the sea. The south of this region consists of lower forests and knolls, with <a href="/wiki/Kirkby_Moor" title="Kirkby Moor">Kirkby Moor</a> on the southern boundary. The southwestern Lake District ends near the <a href="/wiki/Furness" title="Furness">Furness</a> peninsula and <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness" title="Barrow-in-Furness">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, a town which many Lake District residents rely on for basic amenities.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeastern_area">Southeastern area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Southeastern area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The southeastern area is the territory between <a href="/wiki/Coniston_Water" title="Coniston Water">Coniston Water</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a> and east of Windermere towards Kendal and south to Lindale. There are no high summits in this area which is mainly low hills, knolls and limestone <a href="/wiki/Cuesta" title="Cuesta">cuestas</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Gummer%27s_How" title="Gummer&#39;s How">Gummer\'s How</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitbarrow" title="Whitbarrow">Whitbarrow</a>. Indeed, it rises only as high as 333&#160;m (1,093&#160;ft) at <a href="/wiki/Top_o%27_Selside" class="mw-redirect" title="Top o&#39; Selside">Top o\' Selside</a> east of Coniston Water; the wide expanse of <a href="/wiki/Grizedale_Forest" title="Grizedale Forest">Grizedale Forest</a> stands between the two lakes. <a href="/wiki/Kendal" title="Kendal">Kendal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morecambe_Bay" title="Morecambe Bay">Morecambe Bay</a> stand at the eastern and southern edges of the area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lakes">Lakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Lakes">edit</a><span margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Major lakes<b></b></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Only one of the lakes in the Lake District is called by that name, <a href="/wiki/Bassenthwaite_Lake" title="Bassenthwaite Lake">Bassenthwaite Lake</a>. All the others such as <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coniston_Water" title="Coniston Water">Coniston Water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ullswater" title="Ullswater">Ullswater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buttermere" title="Buttermere">Buttermere</a> are meres, <a href="/wiki/Tarn_(lake)" title="Tarn (lake)">tarns</a> and waters, with <i><a href="/wiki/Mere_(lake)" title="Mere (lake)">mere</a></i> being the least common and <i>water</i> being the most common. The major lakes and reservoirs in the National Park are given below.\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bassenthwaite_Lake" title="Bassenthwaite Lake">Bassenthwaite Lake</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brotherswater" class="mw-redirect" title="Brotherswater">Brotherswater</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Buttermere" title="Buttermere">Buttermere</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coniston_Water" title="Coniston Water">Coniston Water</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg/220px-William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg/330px-William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg/440px-William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1070" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Smith_geological_map_of_Cumberland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geological map of Cumberland, by William Smith (1824)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skiddaw_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-Skiddaw_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3236" data-file-height="2428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skiddaw_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skiddaw seen from Derwentwater</div></div></div>\n<p>The Lake District\'s geology is very complex but well-studied.<sup id="cite_ref-Gannon,_Rock_Trails_Lakeland_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gannon,_Rock_Trails_Lakeland-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Batholith" title="Batholith">batholith</a> beneath the area is responsible for this upland massif, its relatively low density causing the area to be "buoyed up". The granite can be seen at the surface as the Ennerdale, Skiddaw, Carrock Fell, Eskdale and Shap granites.\n</p><p>Broadly speaking the area can be divided into three bands, the divisions between which run south west to north east. Generally speaking the rocks become younger from north west to south east. The north western band is composed of early to mid-<a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a> <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a>, largely <a href="/wiki/Mudstone" title="Mudstone">mudstones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siltstone" title="Siltstone">siltstones</a> of marine origin. Together they comprise the <a href="/wiki/Skiddaw_Group" title="Skiddaw Group">Skiddaw Group</a> and include the rocks traditionally known as the <a href="/wiki/Skiddaw_Slate" title="Skiddaw Slate">Skiddaw Slates</a>. Their <a href="/wiki/Friability" title="Friability">friability</a> generally leads to mountains with relatively smooth slopes such as Skiddaw itself.\n</p><p>The central band is a mix of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> and sedimentary rocks of mid-to-late Ordovician age comprising the <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lavas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuff" title="Tuff">tuffs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Borrowdale_Volcanic_Group" title="Borrowdale Volcanic Group">Borrowdale Volcanic Group</a>, erupted as the former <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_Ocean" title="Iapetus Ocean">Iapetus Ocean</a> was <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">subducted</a> beneath what is now the Scottish border during the <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_orogeny" title="Caledonian orogeny">Caledonian orogeny</a>. The northern central peaks, such as Great Rigg, were produced by considerable lava flows. These lava eruptions were followed by a series of <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic</a> eruptions which produced a series of calderas, one of which includes present-day Scafell Pike. These pyroclastic rocks give rise to the craggy landscapes typical of the central fells.<sup id="cite_ref-Gannon,_Rock_Trails_Lakeland_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gannon,_Rock_Trails_Lakeland-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The south eastern band comprises the mudstones and <a href="/wiki/Wacke" class="mw-redirect" title="Wacke">wackes</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Windermere_Supergroup" title="Windermere Supergroup">Windermere Supergroup</a> and which includes (successively) the rocks of the Dent, Stockdale, Tranearth, Coniston and Kendal groups. These are generally a little less resistant to erosion than the rocks sequence to the north and underlie much of the lower landscapes around Coniston and Windermere.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Later <a href="/wiki/Intrusion" class="mw-redirect" title="Intrusion">intrusions</a> have formed individual outcrops of <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">igneous rock</a> in each of these groups.\nAround the edges of these Ordovician and Silurian rocks on the northern, eastern and southern fringes of the area is a semi-continuous outcrop of <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous_Limestone" title="Carboniferous Limestone">Carboniferous Limestone</a> seen most spectacularly at places like <a href="/wiki/Whitbarrow_Scar" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitbarrow Scar">Whitbarrow Scar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scout_Scar" title="Scout Scar">Scout Scar</a>.\n<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_District&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Lake District\'s location on the northwest coast of England, coupled with its mountainous geography, makes it the wettest part of England. The UK <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a> reports average annual <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> of more than 2,000&#160;mm (80&#160;in), but with very large local variation.\n</p><p>Although the entire region receives above average rainfall, there is a wide disparity between the amount of rainfall in the western and eastern lakes, as the Lake District experiences <a href="/wiki/Relief_rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Relief rainfall">relief rainfall</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seathwaite,_Allerdale" title="Seathwaite, Allerdale">Seathwaite, Borrowdale</a> is the wettest inhabited place in England with an average of 3,300&#160;mm (130&#160;in) of rain a year,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> while nearby <a href="/wiki/Sprinkling_Tarn" title="Sprinkling Tarn">Sprinkling Tarn</a> is even wetter, recording over 5,000&#160;mm (200&#160;in) per year; by contrast, Keswick, at the end of <a href="/wiki/Borrowdale" title="Borrowdale">Borrowdale</a> receives 1,470&#160;mm (58&#160;in) every year, and <a href="/wiki/Penrith,_Cumbria" title="Penrith, Cumbria">Penrith</a> (just outside the Lake District) only 870&#160;mm (34&#160;in). March to June tend to be the driest months, with October to January the wettest, but at low levels there is relatively little difference between months.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Although sheltered valleys experience <a href="/wiki/Gale" title="Gale">gales</a> on an average of only five days a year, the Lake District is generally very windy with the coastal areas having 20 days of gales, and the fell tops around 100 days of gales per year. The maritime climate means that the Lake District experiences relatively moderate temperature variations through the year. Mean temperature in the valleys ranges from about 3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (37&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in January to around 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in July. (By comparison, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, at the same latitude, ranges from \xe2\x88\x9210 to 19&#160;\xc2\xb0C (14 to 66&#160;\xc2\xb0F).)\n</p><p>The relatively low height of most of the fells means that, while snow is expected during the winter, they can be free of snow at any time of the year. Normally, significant snow fall only occurs between November and April. On average, snow falls on <a href="/wiki/Helvellyn" title="Helvellyn">Helvellyn</a> 67 days per year. During the year, valleys typically experience 20 days with snow falling, a further 200 wet days, and 145 dry days. Hill fog is common at any time of year, and the fells average only around 2.5 hours of sunshine per day, increasing to around 4.1 hours per day on the coastal plains.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%;
